[2025-09-30 21:08:13] Response:
```python
from typing import List
import copy

def program(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    n = 30
    h = copy.deepcopy(g)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if h[i][j] == 0:
                h[i][j] = g[j][i]
    return h
```

```python
from typing import List, Tuple
import numpy as np  # For easier matrix operations if allowed

def find_zero_positions(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[Tuple[int, int]]:
    """Extract positions of zeros for targeted filling."""
    n = len(g)
    zeros = [(i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(n) if g[i][j] == 0]
    return zeros

    h = [row[:] for row in g]  # Shallow copy sufficient if no nested mutation
    for i, j in positions:
        if 0 <= j < n and 0 <= i < n and g[j][i] != 0:  # Avoid filling with another zero
            h[i][j] = g[j][i]
    return h

def detect_patterns(g: List[List[int]]) -> dict:
    """Identify repetitive rows or blocks for symmetry checks."""
    n = len(g)
    patterns = {}
    for i in range(n):
        row_tuple = tuple(g[i])
        if row_tuple in patterns:
            patterns[row_tuple].append(i)
        else:
            patterns[row_tuple] = [i]
    return {k: v for k, v in patterns.items() if len(v) > 1}  # Only duplicates
```

```python
def find_zero_positions(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[Tuple[int, int]]:
    """Extract positions of zeros for targeted filling."""
    n = len(g)
    zeros = [(i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(n) if g[i][j] == 0]
    return zeros

def transpose_partial(g: List[List[int]], positions: List[Tuple[int, int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    """Attempt partial transpose only on zero positions, but check if g[j][i] != 0 before filling."""
    n = len(g)

        if 0 <= j < n and 0 <= i < n and g[j][i] != 0:  # Avoid filling with another zero
```

```python
from typing import List

def make_transpose_symmetric(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    n = 30
    h = [row[:] for row in g]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            v_lower = h[j][i]
            v_upper = h[i][j]
            if v_lower != 0 or v_upper != 0:
                val = v_lower if v_lower != 0 else v_upper
                h[i][j] = val
                h[j][i] = val
    return h

def apply_row_mirroring(h: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    n = 30
    for k in range(17, n):
        paired = 31 - k
        h[k] = h[paired][:]
    return h

def program(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    h = make_transpose_symmetric(g)
    h = apply_row_mirroring(h)
    return h
```

```python
from typing import List

def make_transpose_symmetric(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    n = 30
    h = [row[:] for row in g]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            v_lower = h[j][i]
            v_upper = h[i][j]
            if v_lower != 0 or v_upper != 0:
                val = v_lower if v_lower != 0 else v_upper
                h[i][j] = val
                h[j][i] = val
    return h

def apply_row_mirroring(h: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    n = 30
    for k in range(17, n):
        paired = 31 - k
        h[k] = h[paired][:]
    return h

def program(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    h = make_transpose_symmetric(g)
    h = apply_row_mirroring(h)
    return h
```

[2025-09-30 21:24:11] Response:
**High level:** This is a visual puzzle where the goal is to transform a partially filled 30x30 grid of digits (0-9, with 0 likely representing empty or unfilled cells) into a completed grid that is symmetric across the main diagonal (i.e., a symmetric matrix where grid[i][j] == grid[j][i]) and also satisfies a specific row-based mirroring symmetry, where the lower rows (17-29) are exact copies of specific upper rows (14 down to 2) after all fillings are propagated.

**Details, subtleties, key considerations:**
 * The grid must be fully filled such that no 0s remain in the output; 0s in the input represent unfilled cells that need to be completed based on symmetry propagation, not left as-is.
 * Transpose symmetry requires that for every pair (i,j) with i < j, the value at [i][j] and [j][i] must be the same; if at least one is non-zero, use that non-zero value (preferring the lower triangle if both non-zero, per the code), but if both are 0, do not leave it 0propagation from row mirroring or multiple symmetry applications is needed to fill it.
 * Row mirroring is not a standard horizontal reflection (e.g., not pairing row i with 29-i); instead, it specifically copies row 14 to row 17, row 13 to row 18, ..., row 2 to row 29, leaving rows 0, 1, 15, and 16 unchanged by this operation. This creates a "shifted" mirroring effect centered around rows 15-16.
 * Full completion requires propagating values across both symmetries iteratively: a value in one position must fill its transpose pair and any mirrored row positions (and their transpose pairs), potentially requiring multiple passes until the grid stabilizes (no further changes). Single-pass application leaves isolated 0s unfilled.
 * Subtlety: The symmetries interact; for example, a non-zero in an upper row can propagate via row mirroring to a lower row, then via transpose to fill a previously zero upper triangle position. Assuming input consistency (no conflicting non-zeros in symmetric positions), use the existing non-zero value.
 * Easy to miss: Rows 15 and 16 act as a "central band" not directly mirrored, but they must still be transpose-symmetric internally and influence propagation. Also, 0s in central or isolated positions (e.g., on the diagonal or in the central band) may require full orbit propagation under the symmetry group generated by transpose and row-mirroring operations.
 * Outputs must be exact matches; even single-cell differences (especially 0 vs. non-zero) cause failure. The grid size is fixed at 30x30.
 * No evidence of other operations like max/min, averaging, or pattern interpolation beyond symmetry propagation; conflicting values aren't handled in examples (assume inputs are consistent).

**Helpful functions, types, and tools:**
```python
from typing import List
from copy import deepcopy

def make_transpose_symmetric(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    """
    Partially helpful: Makes the grid symmetric across the main diagonal by setting h[i][j] = h[j][i] for i < j,
    using the non-zero value if at least one exists (prefers lower triangle). However, it leaves 0s if both are 0,
    which fails propagationcombine with iterative application.
    """
    n = len(g)
    h = [row[:] for row in g]
    changed = False
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            v_lower = h[j][i]
            v_upper = h[i][j]
            if v_lower != 0 or v_upper != 0:
                val = v_lower if v_lower != 0 else v_upper
                if h[i][j] != val or h[j][i] != val:
                    changed = True
                h[i][j] = val
                h[j][i] = val
    return h, changed  # Return changed flag for iteration
```

```python
def apply_row_mirroring(h: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    """
    Helpful: Applies the specific row mirroring by copying upper rows 2-14 to lower rows 29-17 (reversed order).
    This matches the expected structure but must be applied iteratively with transpose symmetry to propagate fillings.
    """
    n = 30
    changed = False
    for k in range(17, n):
        paired = 31 - k  # Maps 17->14, 18->13, ..., 29->2
        if h[k] != h[paired]:
            changed = True
        h[k] = h[paired][:]
    return h, changed  # Return changed flag for iteration
```

```python
def propagate_symmetries(g: List[List[int]]) -> List[List[int]]:
    """
    Suggested helpful tool (not in original): Iteratively apply transpose symmetry and row mirroring until no changes.
    This addresses the unfilled 0s by propagating values across symmetry orbits.
    """
    h = [row[:] for row in g]
    while True:
        h1, changed1 = make_transpose_symmetric(h)
        h2, changed2 = apply_row_mirroring(h1)
        if not (changed1 or changed2):
            break
        h = h2
    return h
```
* No other types or tools provided; no object extraction needed, as this is grid transformation, not object detection.
